     725             : class PaintedLayerDataTree;

     727             : /**
     728             :  * This is tree node type for PaintedLayerDataTree.
     729             :  * Each node corresponds to a different animated geometry root, and contains
     730             :  * a stack of PaintedLayerDatas, in bottom-to-top order.
     731             :  * There is at most one node per animated geometry root. The ancestor and
     732             :  * descendant relations in PaintedLayerDataTree tree mirror those in the frame
     733             :  * tree.
     734             :  * Each node can have clip that describes the potential extents that items in
     735             :  * this node can cover. If mHasClip is false, it means that the node's contents
     736             :  * can move anywhere.
     737             :  * Testing against the clip instead of the node's actual contents has the
     738             :  * advantage that the node's contents can move or animate without affecting
     739             :  * content in other nodes. So we don't need to re-layerize during animations
     740             :  * (sync or async), and during async animations everything is guaranteed to
     741             :  * look correct.
     742             :  * The contents of a node's PaintedLayerData stack all share the node's
     743             :  * animated geometry root. The child nodes are on top of the PaintedLayerData
     744             :  * stack, in z-order, and the clip rects of the child nodes are allowed to
     745             :  * intersect with the visible region or visible above region of their parent
     746             :  * node's PaintedLayerDatas.
     747             :  */

     893             : class ContainerState;

     895             : /**
     896             :  * A tree of PaintedLayerDataNodes. At any point in time, the tree only
     897             :  * contains nodes for animated geometry roots that new items can potentially
     898             :  * merge into. Any time content is added on top that overlaps existing things
     899             :  * in such a way that we no longer want to merge new items with some existing
     900             :  * content, that existing content gets "finished".
     901             :  * The public-facing methods of this class are FindPaintedLayerFor,
     902             :  * AddingOwnLayer, and Finish. The other public methods are for
     903             :  * PaintedLayerDataNode.
     904             :  * The tree calls out to its containing ContainerState for some things.
     905             :  * All coordinates / rects in the tree or the tree nodes are in the
     906             :  * ContainerState's coordinate space, i.e. relative to the reference frame and
     907             :  * in layer pixels.
     908             :  * The clip rects of sibling nodes never overlap. This is ensured by finishing
     909             :  * existing nodes before adding new ones, if this property were to be violated.
     910             :  * The root tree node doesn't get finished until the ContainerState is
     911             :  * finished.
     912             :  * The tree's root node is always the root reference frame of the builder. We
     913             :  * don't stop at the container state's mContainerAnimatedGeometryRoot because
     914             :  * some of our contents can have animated geometry roots that are not
     915             :  * descendants of the container's animated geometry root. Every animated
     916             :  * geometry root we encounter for our contents needs to have a defined place in
     917             :  * the tree.
     918             :  */

    4998             : static void
    4999           0 : FixUpFixedPositionLayer(Layer* aLayer,
    5000             :                         const ActiveScrolledRoot* aTargetASR,
    5001             :                         const ActiveScrolledRoot* aLeafScrollMetadataASR,
    5002             :                         const ActiveScrolledRoot* aContainerScrollMetadataASR,
    5003             :                         const ActiveScrolledRoot* aContainerCompositorASR,
    5004             :                         bool aIsFixedToRootScrollFrame)
    5005             : {
    5006           0 :   if (!aLayer->GetIsFixedPosition()) {
    5007           0 :     return;
    5008             :   }
    5009             : 
    5010             :   // Analyze ASRs to figure out if we need to fix up fixedness annotations on
    5011             :   // the layer. Fixed annotations are required in multiple cases:
    5012             :   //  - Sometimes we set scroll metadata on a layer for a scroll frame that we
    5013             :   //    don't want the layer to be moved by. (We have to do this if there is a
    5014             :   //    scrolled clip that is moved by that scroll frame.) So we set the fixed
    5015             :   //    annotation so that the compositor knows that it should ignore that
    5016             :   //    scroll metadata when determining the layer's position.
    5017             :   //  - Sometimes there is a scroll meta data on aLayer's parent layer for a
    5018             :   //    scroll frame that we don't want aLayer to be moved by. The most common
    5019             :   //    way for this to happen is with containerful root scrolling, where the
    5020             :   //    scroll metadata for the root scroll frame is on a container layer that
    5021             :   //    wraps the whole document's contents.
    5022             :   //  - Sometimes it's just needed for hit testing, i.e. figuring out what
    5023             :   //    scroll frame should be scrolled by events over the layer.
    5024             :   // A fixed layer needs to be annotated with the scroll ID of the scroll frame
    5025             :   // that it is *fixed with respect to*, i.e. the outermost scroll frame which
    5026             :   // does not move the layer. nsDisplayFixedPosition only ever annotates layers
    5027             :   // with the scroll ID of the presshell's root scroll frame, which is
    5028             :   // sometimes the wrong thing to do, so we correct it here. Specifically,
    5029             :   // it's the wrong thing to do if the fixed frame's containing block is a
    5030             :   // transformed frame - in that case, the fixed frame needs to scroll along
    5031             :   // with the transformed frame instead of being fixed with respect to the rsf.
    5032             :   // (It would be nice to compute the annotation only in one place and get it
    5033             :   // right, instead of fixing it up after the fact like this, but this will
    5034             :   // need to do for now.)
    5035             :   // compositorASR is the ASR that the layer would move with on the compositor
    5036             :   // if there were no fixed annotation on it.
    5037             :   const ActiveScrolledRoot* compositorASR =
    5038             :     aLeafScrollMetadataASR == aContainerScrollMetadataASR
    5039             :       ? aContainerCompositorASR
    5040           0 :       : aLeafScrollMetadataASR;
    5041             : 
    5042             :   // The goal of the annotation is to have the layer move with aTargetASR.
    5043           0 :   if (compositorASR && aTargetASR != compositorASR) {
    5044             :     // Mark this layer as fixed with respect to the child scroll frame of aTargetASR.
    5045             :     aLayer->SetFixedPositionData(
    5046             :       ViewIDForASR(FindDirectChildASR(aTargetASR, compositorASR)),
    5047             :       aLayer->GetFixedPositionAnchor(),
    5048           0 :       aLayer->GetFixedPositionSides());
    5049             :   } else {
    5050             :     // Remove the fixed annotation from the layer, unless this layers is fixed
    5051             :     // to the document's root scroll frame - in that case, the annotation is
    5052             :     // needed for hit testing, because fixed layers in iframes should scroll
    5053             :     // the iframe, even though their position is not affected by scrolling in

    6106           0 : static void DrawForcedBackgroundColor(DrawTarget& aDrawTarget,
    6107             :                                       const IntRect& aBounds,
    6108             :                                       nscolor aBackgroundColor)

    6110           0 :   if (NS_GET_A(aBackgroundColor) > 0) {
    6111           0 :     ColorPattern color(ToDeviceColor(aBackgroundColor));
    6112           0 :     aDrawTarget.FillRect(Rect(aBounds), color);
    6113             :   }
    6114           0 : }
    6115             : 
    6116             : /*
    6117             :  * A note on residual transforms:
    6118             :  *
    6119             :  * In a transformed subtree we sometimes apply the PaintedLayer's
    6120             :  * "residual transform" when drawing content into the PaintedLayer.
    6121             :  * This is a translation by components in the range [-0.5,0.5) provided
    6122             :  * by the layer system; applying the residual transform followed by the
    6123             :  * transforms used by layer compositing ensures that the subpixel alignment
    6124             :  * of the content of the PaintedLayer exactly matches what it would be if
    6125             :  * we used cairo/Thebes to draw directly to the screen without going through
    6126             :  * retained layer buffers.
    6127             :  *
    6128             :  * The visible and valid regions of the PaintedLayer are computed without
    6129             :  * knowing the residual transform (because we don't know what the residual
    6130             :  * transform is going to be until we've built the layer tree!). So we have to
    6131             :  * consider whether content painted in the range [x, xmost) might be painted
    6132             :  * outside the visible region we computed for that content. The visible region
    6133             :  * would be [floor(x), ceil(xmost)). The content would be rendered at
    6134             :  * [x + r, xmost + r), where -0.5 <= r < 0.5. So some half-rendered pixels could
    6135             :  * indeed fall outside the computed visible region, which is not a big deal;
    6136             :  * similar issues already arise when we snap cliprects to nearest pixels.
    6137             :  * Note that if the rendering of the content is snapped to nearest pixels ---
    6138             :  * which it often is --- then the content is actually rendered at
    6139             :  * [snap(x + r), snap(xmost + r)). It turns out that floor(x) <= snap(x + r)
    6140             :  * and ceil(xmost) >= snap(xmost + r), so the rendering of snapped content
    6141             :  * always falls within the visible region we computed.
    6142             :  */
    6143             : 
    6144             : /* static */ void
